{~f120v~}\n
{=The text begins immediately below the end of the Ancrene Riwle in Hand\n
A, and slightly less than half way down the folio. The first letter of\n
each verse line is placed in a separately ruled column. Although these\n
are only occasional majuscule in shape, I take the separation to\n
distinguish them as litterae notabiliores and I have therefore\n
designated them as capitals with preceding asterisks=}\n
{\'}\n

# 280\n
{London, British Library, Cotton Otho C xiii, fols 1r-146v: Layamon B}\n
C13b1\n
396 172 N\n
{=NW Wilts=}\n
{=Sample tagged: 1r-19rb=}\n
{=Script - Textura semiquadrata=}\n
{=Status - MS punctuation done; tagging notes and textual notes up to date=}\n
{=Note that the first folio containing the Preface and lines 1-37 are\n
missing as a result of the Cottonian fire. The missing text is\n
supplied in Brook and Leslie (B&L) and in Madden from Wanley\'s\n
transcript. I have not included it here but start from where the\n
MS text now begins. Even so, some of the readings are indecipherable\n
on microfilm and I have had to supply some readings from the editions\n
for the sake of readability, though these supplied readings are not\n
normally tagged. Madden\'s readings which are bracketed in B&L to\n
indicate that they are no longer visible are in square brackets. If\n
they form part of a word that is otherwise legible I occasionally\n
include the word in the tagged text. Otherwise it is excluded by a\n
leading !. Dots indicate illegible text - one dot per letter when\n
close together. When they are spaced, one dot represents an average of\n
two letters - as indicated in B&L. The text is not written in verse lines\n
but as if it is prose. The verse lines in B&L and Madden are editorial.\n
It is not always possible to make out from the microfilm where the MS\n
line endings are. Where I am not certain I give no notice of the line\n
end. I give MS punctuation either from the microfilm, or where it is\n
illegible on film, I follow B&L=}\n
{~f1ra~}\n
{=B&L p7=}\n
